Jamison Brereton

63 (775)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Nidhruvi K─Б┼Ыyapa
30 verses: g─Бyatr─л, arranged in trcas ╠е
Like the last hymn, this one is much concerned with the ritual preparation of soma, but it sketches a larger conceptual world in which this preparation takes place. On the one hand, the purification is seen as a process of ─Аrya-ization (vs. 5), and the spaces that Soma traverses, for example the filter, become тАЬ─Аrya domainsтАЭ (vs. 14). The waters that Soma crosses (vss. 5, 21) and the rivers in which he is groomed (vs. 17) are both the ritual waters in which the soma plant is rinsed and rehydrated and, metaphorically, the frontier rivers the ─Аryas crossed in expanding their realms. (See also the mentions of finding or making тАЬwide spaceтАЭ in the two preceding hymns [IX.61.12; 62.3, 9].)
On the other hand, Soma is compared to and identified with the Sun (espe cially in the third tr╠еca, vss. 7тАУ9, also vs. 13), and his journey across the filter is also metaphorically the SunтАЩs daily journey across the heaven. Since the ritual activity happens on earth, at the hands of Manu (vss. 7тАУ8), the first sacrificer and the cul tural ancestor of the ─Аrya, even the rising of the Sun is thus implicitly attributed to human agency.
The hymn is, of course, also full of requests for material goods of all sorts, and, especially toward the end, for Soma to smite all manner of enemies and hostile forces (vss. 24, 26, 28тАУ29; also 5).
Although the hymn does not seem tightly structured, some tr╠еcas show formal unity (e.g., vss. 25тАУ27 with forms of the root sr╠еj тАЬsurgeтАЭ), and the hymn begins and ends with verses containing the imperative dh─Бraya тАЬsecure, sustain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

61-67 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On the place of these long hymns in the structure of the maс╣Зс╕Нala, see published introduction. to IX.61. All of these hymns consist of collections of tс╣Ыcas of varying degrees of cohesion. In fact, it is surprising how few tс╣Ыcas display a real attempt at thematic or lexical unity, and what they do show is often simply the byproduct of the fact that both the lexicon and thematic preoccupations of Maс╣Зс╕Нala IX are comparatively limited and so similar words and themes are not unlikely to show up in adjacent verses. This lack of unity contrasts, I think (this is my unsystematic and anecdotal impression) with collections of tс╣Ыcas in other maс╣Зс╕Нalas, notably VIII.

English translation:

тАЬPour (upon us), Soma, thousand-fold wealth, with excellent male progeny, secure to us ample food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In purifying yourself, o Soma, bring wealth in thousands and an
abundance of good heroes;
secure our claims to fame for us. с│У

тАЬAugmenting Indra, urging the waters, making all our acts prosperous, destroying the withholders (of oblations).тАЭ

Strengthening Indra, crossing the waters, making it all ─Аrya,
smashing away the non-givers,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бnto v├н┼Ыvam ─Б╠Бryam тАЬmaking it all ─Аrya,тАЭ esp. in conjunction with apt├║raс╕е тАЬcrossing the waters,тАЭ most likely alludes to the ─Аrya expansion in their migration into the northern part of the subcontinent, specifically to crossing frontier rivers and laying claim to the land on the other side. This territorial expansion is implicitly compared here to SomaтАЩs ritual journey. Since, as Geldner notes (n. 5b), the Soma cult is specifically ─Аrya, importing this practice into new lands would be a key part of the process of Arya-ization.

English translation:

тАЬFlow with that stream with which you, Soma, light up the sun, urging on the waters beneficial to man.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself in the very stream with which you made the sun shine, impelling the waters belonging to Manu.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is specifically stated here that the stream of soma тАЬmade the sun shineтАЭ (s┼л╠Бryam ├бrocayaс╕е), in other words that the ritual activity produced cosmic effects.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. In these vss. Soma is compared to the sun, and his ritual journey compared to the SunтАЩs daily journey across the sky. At the same time the purification of the soma is linked with Manu, the first sacrificer (vss. 7-8), and so the cosmic and the ritual are connected.

Flow onward with that stream of thine wherewith thou gavest Surya light,
Urging on waters good to men.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe purified (Soma) harnesses the horse of the sun to travel through the firmament to man.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He has yoked Eta┼Ыa, (the steed) of the Sun, purifying himself in ManuтАЩs presence,
to drive through the midspace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Soma goes from affecting the sun in vs. 7 to identity with the sun in this vs, since he yokes Eta┼Ыa, the sunтАЩs horse, and travels through the midspace as if on the sunтАЩs daily journey - at least in my interpr. and that of Geldner But the vs. can be interpr. in a number of diff. ways, in part because the s┼л╠Бra of the Saс╣Гhit─Б text is multiply ambiguous. If its underlying form is s┼л╠Бraс╕е, per the Pp., it can be either gen./abl. to sv├аr- (so S─Бyaс╣Зa., as well as Geldner and the published translation) or nom. sg. to s┼л╠Бra-; however, it could also be underlying s┼л╠Бre and a loc. to s┼л╠Бra-. (Renou also allows the dat., presumably to sv├аr-, but the only clear dat. to this stem is accented s┼лr├й [IV.3.8]; s┼л╠Бre duhit─Б╠Б[I.34.5] is actually an old gen. with close sandhi effect before dental, likewise in IX.97.38; see my Fs. Melchert article, тАЬS┼л╠Бre Duhit├бr’s Brother, the тАШPlacer of the SunтАЩ: Another Example of -e тЖР*-as in Rigvedic Phrasal Sandhi,тАЭ 2010.). In any case, an underlying s┼л╠Бraс╕е is more likely than s┼л╠Бre because of the s┼л╠Бro in the next vs. (9b), which repeats much of the verbal material in this one.

L├╝ders (215-16) objects to GeldnerтАЩs interpr. of the vs., on the basis that the sun always travels through heaven, and here the travel is through the midspace (ant├бrikс╣гena). So in his view this cannot refer to heavenly Soma identified with the sun, but must refer to the earthly Soma, who takes the name S┼лra (hence s┼л╠Бraс╕е is a nominative for him) and yokes a horse named Eta┼Ыa after the SunтАЩs horse, and journeys towards heaven through the midspace. In other words, his Soma seems as if heтАЩs trying to steal the sunтАЩs identity by stealing his names. I confess that the subtleties of L├╝dersтАЩs distinctions escape me, depending as they do on his strict separation of earthly and heavenly elements throughout his Varuс╣Зa vols. Renou seems to adopt some version of the L├╝ders interpr., judging from his tr. of bc тАЬтАж pour quтАЩil aille du (domaine de) Manu (au ciel) ├а travers lтАЩespace-m├йdian,тАЭ interpr. man─Б╠Бv ├бdhi as if it contained an abl. man├│r before ├бdhi. (He interpr. the same two p─Бdas two hymns later [IX.65.16bc] quite differently.) I do see the point about the midspace, however, and am willing to concede that Soma-as-Sun is not quite as high a flyer as the Sun himself. Bloomfield (RReps ad loc.) also considers s┼л╠Бraс╕е a nom., but in his view this expresses тАЬthe complete assimiliation of Soma Pavam─Бna to the sun,тАЭ which is a different conclusion from L├╝dersтАЩs. The point is surely not whether Soma is literally in heaven, but that he has acquired and displays the salient characteristics of the Sun and is therefore identified with the Sun despite remaining in the ritual arena.

07-09 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. In these vss. Soma is compared to the sun, and his ritual journey compared to the SunтАЩs daily journey across the sky. At the same time the purification of the soma is linked with Manu, the first sacrificer (vss. 7-8), and so the cosmic and the ritual are connected.

Griffith

He, Pavamana, high o’er man yoked the Sun’s courser Etasa
To travel through the realm of air.

Geldner

Der Pavamana hat unter Manu den Etasa der Sonne geschirrt, um durch die Luft zu fahren.

Grassmann

Die Sonne hat ihr Ross geschirrt hellflammend in des Menschen Sitz, Zu fahren durch den Raum der Luft.

English translation:

тАЬAnd Indu exclaiming ‘Indra!’ harnesses the (horse of the) sun to go towards these ten regions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ty─Б harito da┼Ыa: haritaс╕е = horses or rays of the sun

Jamison Brereton

And these ten tawny mares of the Sun he has yoked, to drive,
the drop, announcing, тАЬ(I go) to Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b of this vs., s┼л╠Бro ayukta y─Б╠Бtave, consists entirely of words repeated from the previous vs.; in addition, substituting for ├йta┼Ыam in 8a, we find an expanded horse term, ty─Б╠Б har├нto d├б┼Ыa тАЬthese ten tawny maresтАЭ as obj. of ayukta. Again Soma is being identified with the sun and his ritual journey identified with the sunтАЩs transit; again the cosmic and the ritual are intertwined, for the ten mares are probably both the SunтАЩs horses (as L├╝ders points out, p.

216 n. 4, the Sun is credited with ten yoked horses in I.164.14; cf. also s┼л╠Бryasya har├нtaс╕е in V.29.5) and the ten fingers of the priests that press the soma, exactly so called (har├нto d├б┼Ыa) in IX.38.3.

The third p─Бda (├нndur ├нndra ├нti bruv├бn) presents another set of problems: how much of what precedes ├нti is part of the direct speech and what is the content of the speech? See OldenbergтАЩs clear formulation of these questions. The standard solution is to take the speech as including both words preceding ├нti and to take it as a statement of identity; e.g., GeldnerтАЩs тАЬDer Saft ist IndraтАЭ (sim. Oldenberg, L├╝ders 216 n. 4, Klein DGRV I.407), in part on the basis of a similar TB statement (see Geldner n. 9c), though I donтАЩt think this late parallel should be given much weight. Moreover, IX.6.2 ├нndav ├нndra ├нti тАж, with voc. ├нndo outside of the quotation, shows that the тАШdropтАЩ word does not have to be included in the quotation here. In addition, the sandhi of ├нndra ├нti is ambig.: it can represent nom. ├нndraс╕е with the Pp (and the standard interpr.), but it could also be loc. ├нndre, the choice made by Renou (тАЬтАж en disant ┬л cтАЩest bien (pour aller) ├а Indra ┬╗тАЭ). In conjunction with the journey theme of this tс╣Ыca, I find this interpr.

quite appealing and have adopted it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On this tс╣Ыca see published introduction. In these vss. Soma is compared to the sun, and his ritual journey compared to the SunтАЩs daily journey across the sky. At the same time the purification of the soma is linked with Manu, the first sacrificer (vss. 7-8), and so the cosmic and the ritual are connected.

English translation:

тАЬSprinkle worshipper, upon the woollen fleece the exhilarating (Soma) that has been effused in all directions for V─Бyu and for Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From here sprinkle in circles the soma pressed for V─Бyu, the songs, (the soma) exhilarating to Indra,
onto the sheepтАЩs fleece.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The datives v─Бy├бve тАж ├нndr─Бya of course identify this as a ref. to the morning soma pressing, where both those gods receive the soma, and also echo the same datives (in diff. order) in vs. 3.

If g├нraс╕е opening p─Бda b is an acc. pl. (as seems likely), it is somewhat awkwardly placed between two reff. to soma, sut├бm and matsar├бm, ending their respective p─Бdas (a and b). All the acc.s should be objects of p├бri тАж si├▒cata тАШpour in circlesтАЩ, which obviously fits the soma liquid better than the songs. Probably for this reason Grassmann identifies the form as a voc., the only voc. to the stem, but this certainly does not improve the sense: commanding the songs to pour the soma is appreciably worse than ordering unidentified priests to pour songs as well as soma. ElizarenkovaтАЩs tr. (Language and Style of the Vedic с╣Ъс╣гis, p. 85) exemplifies this awkwardness however unintentionally: тАЬFrom here make libation rounds for V─Бyu, for Indra, of the pressed intoxication, O eulogies (or: O eulogizers), onto the sheep strainer!тАЭ She claims that the root noun g├нr- can be used as an agent (hence her тАЬO eulogizersтАЭ; S─Бyaс╣Зa. and Ludwig also take it as agentive: see Geldner n. 10b), but I know of no such usage of this extremely common noun. On the other hand, the trope of тАЬpouring prayersтАЭ is not rare in the RV, though pouring them onto the fleece strainer is a bit extreme. Renou solves the problem by supplying a separate verb to govern g├нraс╕е (тАЬ├йmettezтАЭ), but this seems a typical cop-out on his part.

As in the previous hymn (see comm. ad IX.62.18), the priests are addressed in the 2nd pl. here (p├бri тАж si├▒cata). See also vs. 19, with the same verb.

O self-purifying Soma, find wealth for us that is difficult to surpass, that is difficult to attain by one who craves it.

English translation:

тАЬSoma, like the radiant sun, when effused flows forth, depositing its juice in the pitcher.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma, like the Sun-god, purifies himself, pressed by stones,
placing his own sap in the tub.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As in the tс╣Ыca vss. 7-9, Soma is again compared to the Sun - but curiously no clear point of comparison between them appears in the vs. The actions attributed to Soma here - purifying himself, being pressed by stones, putting his sap in the tub - are exclusive to him and certainly not characteristic of the Sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again no particular signs of unity. The unmixed (тАЬclearтАЭ ┼Ыukr├б-) soma in 14 is contrasted with the soma mixed with curds (d├бdhy─Б┼Ыir-) in 15.

English translation:

тАЬThese brilliang Soma-juices (flowing) towards the dwellings of respectable (worshippers), effuse food and cattle in a stream of water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Across the ─Аrya domains these clear juices in a stream of truth
have flowed to a prize of cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In vs. 5 during his journey Soma тАЬmade it all ─АryaтАЭ; here he crosses these ─Аrya domains (dh─Б╠Бm─Бny ─Б╠Бry─Б) on his journey to the cowsтАЩ milk. My interpr. takes this first acc. phrase as an acc. of extent, of space traversed, while the acc. in p─Бda c, v─Б╠Бjaс╣Г g├│mantam I take as the goal of akс╣гaran. In the next vs., 15c, pav├нtram ├бti тАЬacross the filterтАЭ has the same function I see for dh─Б╠Бm─Бny ─Б╠Бry─Б here, and in fact the filter may be identified as the ─Аrya domains. By contrast Geldner takes dh─Б╠Бm─Бny ─Б╠Бry─Б as parallel goal to v─Б╠Бjaс╣Г g├│mantam, while Renou characteristically supplies a separate participle (─Бvi┼Ы├бntaс╕е тАЬont occup├йтАЭ) to govern dh─Б╠Бm─Бny ─Б╠Бry─Б. The parallels he cites in the n. do not seem sufficient to me.

тАЬThe Soma-juices mixed with curds effused for Indra, the wielder of the thunderbolt, flow through the filter.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬSprinkle upon the woollen fleece for Indra the most sweet (Soma), desiring battle as if in battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As if sprinkling a prize-seeking (horse) when the prize (is set), sprinkle prize-seeking (soma) in circles onto the sheepтАЩs fleece,
(the soma) most honeyed for Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains a fairly clever double meaning: the verb p├бri тИЪsic means тАШsprinkle around / in circlesтАЩ. When soma is the object, as it generally is, it refers to the sprinkling of the drops of soma; in other words, the acc. expresses the material that is being sprinkled. But here in the simile v─Б╠Бje n├б v─Бjay├║m, the acc. v─Бjay├║m тАШprize-seekingтАЩ refers to a horse in a race or contest, which would be the target or the goal of the sprinkling, with some type of liquid being sprinkled upon it. The word play is cleverer still, in that v─Бjay├║m should be read twice, both as referring to the horse in the simile and to soma, which is elsewhere modified by this word (e.g., IX.44.4 s├б naс╕е pavasva v─Бjay├║с╕е), in the frame.

Both Geldner and Renou construe v─Б╠Бje in the simile rather loosely; I take it as a unmarked loc. absol. of the dh├бne hit├й (тАЬwhen the prize is set,тАЭ e.g., IX.53.2) type, though without overt ppl. It adds to the somewhat slant syntax of the simile versus the frame that both contain a loc. (├бvyo v─Б╠Бreс╣гu in the frame), but the locc. have different functions. In fact ├бvyo v─Б╠Бreс╣гu тАЬonto the sheepтАЩs fleeceтАЭ expresses the goal of the sprinkling and is functionally parallel to v─Бjay├║m in the simile.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca has more internal unity, as well as connection to the preceding tс╣Ыca, than usual. For its external connections, see 19a v─Б╠Бje n├б v─Бjay├║m picking up the v─Бj- forms just noted, m├бdhumattamam in 19c matching the same word (in the nom.) in 16a, and 20a kav├нm mс╣Ыjanti echoing 17a t├бm ─л mс╣Ыjanti (note the identical vowel pattern in kav├нm / t├бm ─л).

As for internal connections, see dh─лbh├нс╕е (20b, 21a), v├нpr─Бс╕е (20b, 21c), and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б (20c), vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зam (221a).

For battle as it were in war.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe (worshippers) desiring protection, cleanse with their fingers the purifiable (Soma) the sage; with a noise the sprinkler (of benefits) flows forth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The inspired poets, seeking help, with their insights groom the sage poet worthy to be groomed.
The bull rushes ever roaring.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note kav├нm (of Soma) contrasting with v├нpr─Бс╕е, the human poets who groom him.

This tс╣Ыca has more internal unity, as well as connection to the preceding tс╣Ыca, than usual. For its external connections, see 19a v─Б╠Бje n├б v─Бjay├║m picking up the v─Бj- forms just noted, m├бdhumattamam in 19c matching the same word (in the nom.) in 16a, and 20a kav├нm mс╣Ыjanti echoing 17a t├бm ─л mс╣Ыjanti (note the identical vowel pattern in kav├нm / t├бm ─л).

As for internal connections, see dh─лbh├нс╕е (20b, 21a), v├нpr─Бс╕е (20b, 21c), and vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б (20c), vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зam (221a).

English translation:

тАЬThe wise (priests) in a stream of water send forth with their fingers, and with praise the sprinkler (of benefits), the shedder of water.тАЭ

To the water-crossing bull, Soma, in a stream of truth
have the inspired poets cried out in unison with their insights, their
thought. с│У

тАЬSoma, you who are exhilarating flow defeating the enemies, bestowing knowledge (on us); drive off the people who love not the gods.тАЭ

Smashing away the scorners, you purify yourself, finding the resolve, exhilarating, o Soma.
Thrust from yourself the people who do not seek the gods. с│У

This tс╣Ыca shows clear signs of unity, indeed of a monotonous sort. Like the previous tс╣Ыca, each vs. in this one contains a form of p├бva-, but in this tс╣Ыca all three are the nom. pl. part. p├бvam─Бn─Б(s─Б)с╕е, always opening the vs. Each vs. also contains one finite verb, an augmented form of тИЪsс╣Ыj (asс╣Ыkс╣гata 25a, 27b; asс╣Ыgram 26b). The first two vss. also contain nom. pl. ├нndavaс╕е in the same metrical position (final in the b p─Бda). The lexeme ├бpa тИЪhan found in the previous tс╣Ыca (apaghn├бn 24a) also reappears here (26c ghn├бntaс╕е тАж ├бpa) (and in the next tс╣Ыca).
